The Fifth Session Today

North China Games Open in Jinan 104

Over a Thousand Male and Female Athletes Compete for Fourteen Championships

Men's and Women's Track and Field Begin Today, Intermediate Tennis Begins

Next Session: Tianjin Merges with Hebei, Xinjiang and Ningxia Added as Units

Han Fuqu Hosts Banquet for Athletes, Team Leaders, etc. at Meeting Yesterday

The Fifth North China Games will grandly open in Jinan this morning, lasting four days and closing on the 30th. Participants include eleven units, with over a thousand male and female athletes competing for a total of fourteen championships in the men's senior and intermediate divisions and the women's division. Over 100,000 yuan was spent on the sports field, specially built for this session of the Games. What a grand and successful event! North China's track and field has long been famous. During the Games, numerous national records will surely be broken one by one. Let's wait and see the good news.

Over 100,000 Yuan for Sports Field 105

The various parts of the sports field, such as the field event area, track event area, volleyball and tennis courts, grandstands on all sides, the podium, the military bandstand, and offices, are all brand new, solemn, and magnificent. According to statistics, from March 24th to May 20th, 58 days were spent on construction. The original budget for labor and materials was 74,000 yuan, but it was insufficient, requiring a total of 100,080,000 yuan, exceeding the budget by 34,000 yuan.

Eleven Units Join 106

Total Number of Male and Female Athletes: 1,034

Participants in this North China Games include eleven units: Liaoning, Shanxi, Henan, Hebei, Suiyuan, Chahar, Shandong, Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, and the Harbin District. Statistics confirm that the total number of athletes is 1,034 (including men's and women's track and field and ball games). There are a total of eleven team leaders, twenty-nine instructors, and ninety-three referees for various championships in the competition department.

Fourteen Championships at the Games 107

There are a total of fourteen championships at the Games. Six for men's senior level: (1) Field Events, (2) Track Events, (3) All-Around, (4) Volleyball, (5) Tennis, (6) Baseball. Four for men's intermediate level: (1) Field Events, (2) Track Events, (3) Volleyball, (4) Tennis. Four for the women's division: (1) Track and Field, (2) Volleyball, (3) Tennis, (4) Softball. The men's football and basketball games were previously held in Beiping, so they are not included here.

Opening Ceremony This Morning 108

1. All staff and athletes gather and stand in silence. 2. Cannons are fired (sixteen shots). 3. The flag is raised (music is played). 4. The Party song is sung (music is played). 5. Three bows are made to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen. 6. The chairman respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will, and everyone reads it aloud. 7. Three minutes of silence. 8. The chairman gives the opening address. 9. All athletes take the oath. 10. A representative of the Central Party Headquarters gives a speech. 11. A representative of the Chairman of the National Government gives a speech. 12. Honorary Chairman and Honorary Vice-Chairman give speeches. 13. The Chairman of the Games gives a speech. 14. The Vice-Chairman of the Games gives a speech. 15. The Chief Referee gives a speech. 15. The Chief Referee gives a speech. 16. The Chairman of the Preparatory Committee reports on the preparatory process. 17. Speeches. 18. Chanting of slogans. 19. Photograph. 20. Officials and athletes march around the field (music is played). 21. The Games begin.

Ball Game Competitions Changed to Single Round Robin 113

The original rules for ball game competitions were that double round-robin would be used for teams of three. The competition department of the North China Preparatory Committee previously held a meeting to discuss changing the rules to a single round-robin format. At the time, it was considered a major matter, and it was decided to submit it to the Competition Committee for handling. Only three of the seven members of the Competition Committee were in Jinan: Li Wenchang, Shang Shumei, and Zhang Yixian, which was less than half. They contacted the other four members, Zhang Boling, Yuan Dunli, Hao Gengsheng, and Shou Yi, to seek their consent. Today, replies have been received from Hao and Dong, fully agreeing to the change in the competition rules. This matter has now been approved by a majority of the Competition Committee.

Joint Meeting of the Preparatory Committee and Instructors 116

Zhang Boling Encourages Referees

Jinan, 26th: At 3:00 PM today, a joint meeting of all team leaders, members of the Preparatory Committee, directors, and unit instructors was held. He Siyuan, the chairman, reported on the purpose of the meeting. The directors of the Preparatory Committee reported on the progress of the preparations. Zhang Boling gave a speech, stating that the preparations for this session were very complete and that the first step had been completed. The second step depends entirely on the referees: they must be responsible and impartial, and anyone who does not accept the referee's decision will be disqualified from participating in North China. If this is done, the Games will be a complete success.

Referees' Group Meetings 117

Next Session: Tianjin Merges with Hebei

Xinjiang and Ningxia Added as Units

Jinan, 26th: The referees held group meetings today. The field events committee stipulated various standards. The preparatory meeting of the Sports Federation decided that in the next North China Games, Tianjin will merge with Hebei, and Xinjiang and Ningxia will be added as units. Whether Weihai will join is still undecided. A new regulation was passed stipulating that each province and city will have three representatives with voting rights and that each unit will contribute 1,000 yuan in expenses. A full-time staff member will be established, following the model of the National Sports Federation.

Han Fuqu's Banquet for All Staff 118

Han Fuqu, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, hosted a banquet for all staff members of the North China Games at the podium of the Games venue this morning (the 24th) at 9:00 AM, with a total of 102 attendees. All important figures from the Shandong provincial government, party, and military attended, and Jin Yun'e and representatives from the gentry and business communities, such as He Chunjiang, Ma Liang, and Xin Zhu, were also invited as guests. The atmosphere was extremely jovial. First, Han Fuqu stood up and gave a speech, saying that he was an outsider to sports and didn't have much knowledge about it, but after returning from the National Conference in Nanjing, he saw that the preparations for the North China Games were generally very good and complete, and everyone had worked very hard. The most important thing now is the hospitality. Since the Games are being held in Shandong, we are the hosts, and the guests are coming to us. We should always let them come and go in high spirits and not disappoint them. He hoped that everyone would continue to work hard with the same spirit as before and pay special attention to hospitality. Next, Zhang Honglie, the vice-chairman and director of the Department of Construction, reported on the supplementary measures for groups entering the venue, and Yang Peng, the director of the hospitality section, reported on the detailed hospitality measures, stating that the responsibility for hospitality lies with those responsible for the venue. Hospitality has already been 90% successful, and he hoped that everyone would work hard to complete it. Anyone who sees anything that can be improved can raise it at any time. Next, Jin Yun'e gave a speech, generally hoping that sports would make universal progress. Finally, He Siyuan, the director of the Department of Education, gave a speech, saying that the Games could be divided into three parts: the engineering department, which has now been completed; the administrative department, which has been largely prepared; and the competition department, which has specialized personnel responsible for it. He hoped that everyone would continue to work hard to ensure that the Games have a successful outcome from beginning to end. The banquet ended at 12:00 PM with great pleasure.

No Admission Fee 121

Grand Send-off for Liaoning Athletes 126

(Fast Mail from Fanyang, 23rd) The 135 male and female athletes from Liaoning attending the North China Games departed from the Beining Road on the 23rd of this month. The team leader is Cui Litang, an inspector from the Department of Education, and the general secretary is Zhang Tieshan. He also emphasized the importance of respecting sportsmanship and adhering to the rules, not forgetting politeness in competition. At 8:00 AM the next morning (the 23rd), all the athletes, except for those from Fengyong University who boarded the train at the Japanese station, gathered at the Liaoning General Station to take roll call and board the train. The Beining Road had specially allocated two third-class passenger cars with white paper strips reading "Liaoning North China Athletes Special Car" attached. The athletes were all energetic and cheerful, and the platform was quite lively. At 9:50 AM, the athletes' special car departed westward in the cheers of the crowd. Due to the fact that the provincial government only allocated 8,000 yuan for this participation in the North China Games, which was not enough in reality, the regulations for the athletes' food and accommodation are now such that one yuan in cash is issued per person per day. However, the athletes from Northeastern University are the most favored by the school, receiving a subsidy of ten yuan in cash per person as an encouragement. The school's student union also invited the athletes to a luncheon at the school's club at 7:30 AM on the 23rd to bid them farewell.

Among them, large-scale oil paintings depicting the facts of the Party and the country were particularly noticed by all sectors. The Central Party Headquarters and the National Government will separately preserve and hang part of these oil paintings in the auditorium to commemorate the meritorious service of the founding fathers of the Party and the country. The school's staff in Kyoto will send the portrait of Sun Yat-sen painted by Cai William, the pilgrimage painted by Lin Fengmian, and the paintings "Ten Years to Grow Trees, a Hundred Years to Cultivate People" to the National Government, and the painting "Light of the Nation" painted by Wu Dayu to the Central Party Headquarters.

Baoshan County Elementary School 132

First Joint Meeting of Teachers and Staff 133

The teachers and staff of the Baoshan County Elementary School held their first joint meeting at the First Elementary School yesterday morning. There were 96 attendees, including Yang Hao. Zhang Pinglong was elected as chairman, and after the customary formalities, the discussion began. The resolutions of the various proposals are recorded as follows: (1) Request the Education Bureau to send personnel to supervise the elementary school graduation examination. (2) Request the Education Bureau to deduct the absence fees of the supervisors and teachers and allocate them to teachers' and staff bonuses. (3) From the 20th academic year, request the Education Bureau to increase the salaries of teachers and staff in elementary schools by 30% according to the salary increase standards for social education institutions and normal school principals. (4) Teachers and staff should be assigned 800 to 1,000 minutes of classes; those exceeding this standard should receive additional salaries. (5) The next joint meeting will be held after the summer vacation begins. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

The Anniversary of the May 30th Incident Is Approaching 136

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Makes Preparations for Land and Water Defense

The anniversary of the May 30th Tragedy is approaching rapidly. Chen, the director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, in order to maintain public order, has made special preparations in advance. He has ordered inspectors, police squads, and female inspectors of the bureau to be stationed at locations along the border between the Chinese and French areas, such as Dadongmen, Xinlao Beimen, Xinqiao Street, Fangbanqiao, and Laoximen, to pay attention to inspections. Actively Raising Funds for Relief in Jiangxi 137

Xiong Shihui Hosted People from All Walks of Life Yesterday

Donations of 115,000 Yuan Were Made on the Spot

The Presidium and Committee Members Were Elected

Xiong Shihui, the Garrison Commander of Songhu, initiated the organization of the Jiangxi Disaster Relief Fundraising Association due to the severity of the disaster in Jiangxi. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, Xiong hosted people from all walks of life at the Bank Association Club on Hong Kong Road. About 200 people attended, including Qian Xinzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Huang Jinrong, Yu Zhiqing, Xu Shiying, Li Zushan, and Guo Waifeng. Xiong and the heads of various departments of the garrison personally greeted them. During the meeting, Xiong reported the purpose of the tea party, saying that the disaster in Jiangxi was unprecedented and hoped that all sectors of society would show deep sympathy and generously donate. Subsequently, Xu Shiying reported on the tragic situation of the disaster in Jiangxi. Immediately afterwards, executive committee members and the presidium were elected. In addition to the guests who attended yesterday's meeting as initiators of the disaster relief association, the presidium included Commander Xiong, Mayor Zhang, Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Huang Jinrong, Wen Lantong, and Wang Xiaolai. Chu Huiseng and 39 others were elected as standing committee members, Zhang Gongquan and 3 others as economic committee members, Li Yunshu, Li Zushan and 96 others as executive committee members, and Shi Liangcai, Wang Boqi and others as propaganda committee members. Finally, Du Yuesheng and others initiated an impromptu donation drive. Xiong donated 10,000 yuan as the first donation, Du Yuesheng donated 30,000 yuan, and Wang Yiting donated 5,000 yuan. All the guests enthusiastically donated, and the total amount raised on the spot reached 115,000 yuan. The meeting dispersed at about 6:00 PM. After the tea party, a standing committee meeting was held, and Tang Feiyu was appointed as the secretary of the relief association. All donations from all sectors of society were designated to be collected by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Red Cross Society, and the Jisheng Association. It was also decided that the second standing committee meeting would be held at 4:00 PM tomorrow afternoon.

Social Affairs Bureau

Handling Disputes in the Sand and Gravel Industry 141

Ordered to Cancel Company Names and Stop Reckless Actions

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has repeatedly received reports from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Sand and Gravel Industry Association stating that the sand and gravel industry in the city is contracted by two companies from Zhejiang Province, Dachang and Yitai. They frequently impose harsh taxes on sand and mud and use high-pressure tactics such as detaining goods and people, leading to a city-wide shutdown. They requested that measures be taken to mediate to avoid escalating unrest and affecting commerce. The bureau immediately reported the situation to the Municipal Government and forwarded it to the Zhejiang Provincial Government for verification. After investigation by the bureau, it was confirmed to be true. It was also found that the two tax-contracting companies, Dachang and Yitai, had not registered and falsely claimed to be companies, which violated Article 18 of the General Rules for Merchants. Furthermore, the Zhejiang contractors arbitrarily set up checkpoints in the city to collect taxes, infringing on the administrative authority of the city, and also detained goods and people, leading to strikes, which had a significant impact on the construction industry and the livelihoods of laborers. This should be corrected to prevent the escalation of unrest. Therefore, in addition to ordering the two companies, Dachang and Yitai, to cancel their company names before registering, a document was submitted to the Municipal Government to order the Public Security Bureau to instruct the districts under its jurisdiction to strictly stop any detention of goods and people to prevent disputes and ensure commercial stability.

Social Affairs Bureau's Approval: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday approved the Sand and Gravel Industry Association's request to stop the levying of sand and mud production and sales taxes. Both reports have been received, and the Municipal Government has been requested to order the Public Security Bureau to instruct its subordinates to stop it. This is the approval.

Boatmen's Statement: Yao Wencan and other boatmen from the Shaoxing Sailboat Office submitted a report to the Supervisory Yuan yesterday, stating that they are requesting an investigation into the fabricated names, deceptive rhetoric, contracting, and disguised likin-like sand and mud management fees that are being levied arbitrarily and severely burdening merchants, in order to warn against imitation and stabilize commerce. Yao Wencan and other boatmen specialize in transporting sand and mud. In the past, when collecting sand and mud from Ningbo and other places, they paid a land price of 22 cents per ton and also paid education donations and police fees. The selling price in Shanghai was 2.1 yuan per ton. They risked the dangers of wind and waves with their hard work to earn meager profits to make a living. However, recently, Wu Yousan and others, the principals of the two companies Dachang and Yitai, disregarded the livelihoods of our boat industry and contracted for harsh taxes from the Construction Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, using deceptive rhetoric and fabricated names, calling it a "management fee." Initially, the fee was 1 yuan per ton, but due to public anger and disagreement, it was changed to 70 cents per ton. They also set up checkpoints at important passes in Jiangsu Province and Shanghai Municipality to levy donations and threatened in various ways. Yao Wencan and others are all poor boat merchants who cannot bear this heavy burden. Moreover, sand and mud are a kind of waste material used to benefit people, and the boatmen's transportation can dredge rivers. There is no need for management. It is not necessary for the bureau to manage the sand and mud that is used as waste material to implement the State Council's policy of showing consideration for the difficulties of merchants and abolishing likin. The contracting system has long been abolished. How can this kind of sand and mud management fee, which is a disguised form of likin and taxes goods, not only violate the political program but also go against the original intention of abolishing likin? Furthermore, the contracting of this tax by the two companies Dachang and Yitai is a disregard for government orders. Wencan and others are forced to present this urgent report due to livelihood concerns. We sincerely request your inspection and ask you to severely investigate and deal with it in order to warn against imitation and stabilize commerce. We respectfully request your approval and are extremely grateful. Respectfully presented to the Supervisory Yuan of the National Government by Yao Wencan, Fu Dingsen, Yao Yongtai, and other boatmen from the Shaoxing Sailboat Office.

Construction Industry's Telegram: The Shanghai Construction Industry Association telegraphed the National Government's Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance yesterday regarding the issue of the Construction Department of Zhejiang Province levying sand and mud donations and the shutdown of the sand and gravel industry, requesting a prompt abolition to stabilize commerce. The text of the telegram is as follows: Respectfully submitted, since the Construction Department of Zhejiang Province increased the sand and mud donation, the sand and gravel industry unanimously went on strike on May 19th to resist. Although they were persuaded to resume work by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Sand and Gravel Association, the suffering of the merchants will not be relieved until these harsh taxes are abolished. Our association and the sand and gravel industry are interdependent and share the same pain. If these harsh taxes are not abolished soon, causing a second strike, it will inevitably affect the livelihoods of more than 100,000 workers in our industry. Therefore, we urgently request the Executive Yuan and the Ministry to promptly forward this to the Zhejiang Provincial Government for abolition to stabilize commerce. This would be a great service.

Butchers Opened for Business Yesterday 142

Demanding the Abolition of the Technician Inspection Fee

Establishing a Public Welfare Fund Committee

After mediation by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce on the issue of the municipal slaughter tax, the fresh meat industry resumed importing goods and opened for business yesterday. Yesterday, the butchers from the four suburban districts demanded the abolition of the technician inspection fee and the prompt establishment of a public welfare fund committee. The situation yesterday is recorded below.

Opening for Business: After the Municipal Chamber of Commerce resolved the slaughter tax issue two days ago and decided on two solutions, the fresh meat industry prepared to import goods and open for business. Xuejia浜 and Nan Gong宰作 in the southern district of Shanghai slaughtered more than 360 fresh pigs the night before yesterday. Fresh meat was available in the southern district of Shanghai yesterday, and residents, who had not eaten meat for a long time, rushed to buy meat after hearing that it had opened for business. The stores were very crowded and all were sold out by the afternoon. The Hubbei Slaughterhouse on Minli Road in the northern district of Shanghai slaughtered more than 200 fresh pigs last night, and the slaughterhouses in the four suburban districts slaughtered more than 200 fresh pigs. Fresh meat will also be available this morning.

Technician Inspection Fee: The monthly technician inspection fee paid by the fresh meat industry in the four suburban districts is 170 yuan for the seven locations of Yangjing, Yangjiadu, Tangqiao, Xujiahui, Beixinjing, Zhenru, and Jiangwan, 150 yuan for Gaoqiao, and 75 yuan for Yinhang. Now that the slaughter tax issue has been resolved, the purchase of tickets at 39 cents per pig as stipulated by the municipal government has already increased the burden. However, the technician inspection fee has not been abolished. Since there is already a post-slaughter inspection fee, the technician fee is unnecessary. They have requested the industry association to submit a request to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and forward it to the municipal government for abolition to ease the burden on merchants. It is reported that the association will submit a request to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and forward it to the municipal government for abolition.

Public Welfare Funds: The fresh meat merchants in the north and south of Shanghai and the four suburban districts demanded that the industry association promptly establish a public welfare fund management committee and explain the purpose and amount of the funds so that they can be made public, as the amount of public welfare funds allocated by the municipal government from tax revenue in the resolution method has not been determined.

Pigs Ships Arrive in Shanghai: After hearing that the slaughter tax issue had been resolved, Zhang Fuchen and other 1,326 pig merchants from Jiangbei telegraphed various places in Jiangbei to load pigs and send them to Shanghai as soon as possible. Seven pig ships arrived the day before yesterday and six arrived yesterday, which is quite different from normal times.

Mining Federation

Appeal for Reduced Freight Rates 143

The China Mining Federation, located at No. 38 Edward Road in Shanghai, recently submitted a document to the Ministry of Industry to appeal for relief from the increased freight rates on the Jiaoji, Jinpu, Pinghan, and Pingsui railways. The original manuscript of the document is found as follows: "Respectfully submitted to request the maintenance of low freight rates for domestic coal to save the mining industry and benefit the people. We respectfully request your approval and forwarding. The progress of industry depends entirely on power, and coal is the most important fuel for power. Low coal prices reduce production costs, industry is easier to develop, national productivity increases, and the people can benefit from it. China's coal deposits are extremely rich, but those operated purely with Chinese capital are mostly weak in financial resources. Even the larger mines only produce 2,000 to 3,000 tons per day, while mines operated with foreign capital are strong in financial resources and produce more than 10,000 tons per day. The disparity in strength is difficult to compete with. In addition, Chinese-funded coal mines have been on the verge of bankruptcy due to the impact of military affairs over the years, and coal prices have been soaring, causing the industrial sector to suffer from expensive fuel. There have been frequent calls for help. Now that military affairs have been quelled, the National Government is working hard to govern and renew the people. The Ministry of Railways convened a commercial transportation meeting to establish fair principles. All our merchants and people are grateful. The resolution principles of the commercial transportation meeting are as follows: (1) The freight rate for domestic coal per catty should be based on the lowest possible range of transportation costs for each railway and coal production costs and sales prices for each mine. There is also a resolution to convene a mining committee. If the government establishes an active relief and incentive policy for our country's mining industry and industry, which urgently need relief and incentives, even if the railway depreciates in value, it would not be excessive. However, the Mining Transportation Committee has not yet been convened, and how railway costs are calculated is still unclear to the public. The Jiaoji Railway suddenly issued an order to increase freight rates by 20% from May 1st, and the Jinpu, Pinghan, and Pingsui railways also issued an order to increase coal freight rates by 15% from May 1st. The mines of our federation are all panic-stricken. Moreover, the abolition of unequal treaties is the legacy of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen. However, foreign coal still relies on its unequal treaties to enjoy the right to special reduced freight rates, while the freight rates for domestic coal are arbitrarily increased by various railways, which will inevitably destroy the mining industry operated with Chinese capital and curb the development of industry. We hope that your ministry will promote industry and be considerate of the difficulties of merchants in every possible way. We ask that you consider that the use of coal is of great importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood, and allow us to forward this to the Ministry of Railways to order all railways to stop increasing coal transportation and quickly convene the Mining Transportation Committee for further deliberation.

Purchasing Foreign Rice and Wheat 144

Must Register with the Social Affairs Bureau

In order to regulate the people's food supply and protect the grain market, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has organized the registration of import grain sales. The regulations have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and forwarded to the Executive Yuan for record. The registration of imported rice and wheat has been launched and grain industry associations have been ordered to comply. Yesterday, a summary of the registration procedures was also announced to the grain industry associations. The announcement is recorded below. Announcement: In order to regulate the people's food supply and protect the grain market, this bureau has organized the registration of import grain sales and has formulated regulations that have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and forwarded to the Executive Yuan for record. The registration of imported rice and wheat has also been launched and grain industry associations have been ordered to comply. In addition to the registration regulations being announced and implemented after approval by the Executive Yuan, a summary of the registration procedures is listed below. It is hoped that all grain merchants will comply. Hereafter, un-registered sales contracts and purchase orders will not be allowed to be traded in the market, and violators will be punished. There is no charge for the registration mentioned above. This is for your information. (1) All merchants in this city who purchase foreign rice and wheat should immediately obtain a registration application form from the association, fill it out according to the format, and sign and stamp it. (2) After filling out the application form, it should be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau along with the deposit slip for registration. (3) After receiving the application form, the Social Affairs Bureau will review it and, if there are no errors, stamp the sales contract and return it, allowing it to be traded in the market. (4) After the imported foreign rice and wheat arrives, the applicant should send the verified sales contract along with the bill of lading to the Social Affairs Bureau for verification and registration, and stamping, before being allowed to take delivery.

Departmental Order

Urging Fishermen to Form Fishermen's Associations Quickly 145

Does Not Conflict with Fishery Associations

The Shanghai County Government received an order from the Department of Agriculture and Mines yesterday, stating that in order to comply with the Ministry of Industry's Order No. 11, the organization of fishermen's associations is to seek the common interests of fishermen and fish merchants, and to assist the government in fishery administration facilities, which is extremely important for the development of fisheries. Since the promulgation of the Fishermen's Association Law, few provinces in fishing areas have been organized and established in accordance with the law and reported to the ministry for record. This is not the intention of the national legislation to rectify the fishery industry. Hereafter, in areas where fishermen's associations have not been organized, the departments should instruct their subordinates to urge fishermen to organize them as soon as possible in order to work together to advance the fishery industry. In addition to separate orders, we hereby order the County Government to urge fishermen to organize fishermen's associations as soon as possible and report within two months of the arrival of this document for inspection. This is the order.

Another order stated that in order to comply with the Ministry of Industry's Order No. 1298, the Department telegraphed an inquiry as to whether fish merchants would still be allowed to form trade associations after joining the fishermen's association. The reply stated that after reading the telegram, Article 2 of the Implementing Rules for Trade Association Law is a general mandatory provision, and fish merchants are naturally not an exception. Moreover, the members of the fishermen's association are individuals, and the members of the trade association are companies. Since the two organizations are different and the qualifications for membership are also different, it is legally permissible for fish merchants to organize a trade association even after joining the fishermen's association. Please inform the County Government to inform the County Fishermen's Association and Fishery Organizations. This is the order.

The Military Law Tribunal Received Various Cases for Review Yesterday 146

A Total of Seventeen Communist Cases

First Trial This Friday

The Shanghai Provisional Military Law Tribunal has been in operation for many days since it began work. Yesterday morning, the Military Law Department of the Garrison Headquarters transferred important Communist and counter-revolutionary cases, including the Liu Shaoxiu case and the conspiracy to assassinate the National Government's military advisor, a total of seventeen cases, to the tribunal for trial. Presiding Judge Chen Hanzuo and Investigating Officers Jiang Huaisu, Huang Daolin, Qian Chengjun, and Dai Yuanchuan checked the cases clearly and scheduled them for trial in stages. It has been agreed that the collegiate bench will be convened every Tuesday and Friday for interrogation. However, the number of judges present during the interrogation must exceed the legal majority. After the case is judged, it will be immediately reported to the Military Law Department of the Garrison Headquarters for approval and execution. It has been decided that the first trial will be held this Friday (29th) morning, and the interrogation time will be the Communist Liu Shaoxiu case.

Echoes of the Recovery of the French Concession's Court 147

Telegram from Organizations in the French Concession

Citizens' organizations in the French Concession telegraphed the government yesterday, stating: (Titles Omitted) Our government has decided to recover the French Concession's Court in order to unify jurisdiction, and all Chinese people are applauding. However, the French authorities hope to preserve their only position and interests in China through a policy of appeasement, especially regarding the French Concession's Joint Court. Since the Public Concession implemented the recovery of the Provisional Court, the French Concession's Court has automatically reorganized, and all civil and criminal cases involving Chinese people are tried by Chinese and French judges alone. However, the appointment of judges must still be approved by the French Consul-General. All judgments are accompanied by French consuls if they involve French lawyers, and Chinese lawyers who are not familiar with French cannot represent parties in court. All official documents are still mainly in French, and the name of the French Concession's Court remains the same. This kind of reorganization is actually empty. The Chinese people in our French Concession have suffered deeply from the Public Court, and for the sake of our own interests, we deeply admire the fundamental recovery and substantial reorganization advocated by the Ministry and pledge our support as citizens. We hope that the authorities will be decisive and unwavering, and we will not give up until the goal is achieved. We hereby submit this telegram and respectfully request your inspection and implementation. American Church Investigation Experts Arrive in Shanghai 154

The Da Mei Evening News reports that experts from the New York Society for Religious Studies, both male and female, commissioned by the Foreign Missions Investigation Committee of Christian Believers, have arrived in Shanghai yesterday (25th) after being commissioned to investigate the missionary situation in China, Japan, and India. They will stay for one month to conduct on-site investigations of the work of various American churches and report to the New York Christian Believers Foreign Missions Investigation Committee. This investigation is managed by Mr. Fisher and divided into three groups: China, Japan, and India. The China group consists of ten people, and their investigation work focuses solely on facts without subjective opinions, and is expected to be completed in two and a half years. The motivation is due to the fact that believers who have been donating funds for foreign missions want to know the truth about the work of American churches in China, Japan, and India, so they commissioned experts from the college to conduct a sympathetic investigation.

Important Navigation News 156

Dispute at the Datong Shipping Bureau: A Japanese man named Fuji Naga leased several ships, including the Dalong Maru, Hailong Maru, Pengyang Maru, and Fupu Maru, from Tanaka Trading Company in Japan to operate coastal routes in China. He established the Datong Shipping Company on Renji Road and appointed Zhuang as the Chinese manager. It is now reported by the Japanese-language newspaper Hebun that since the company's establishment, some individuals seeking to become ship stewards have contacted a certain Chinese person in the company and paid a deposit of 5,000 yuan. Now, because the ship has not arrived for a long time, those who paid the deposit are clamoring for the company to return their money, leading to a major dispute. The Japanese consulate has become aware of this matter and is secretly investigating it.

Guangji Ship Has Been Towed Out: The China Merchants Bureau's Guangji ship ran aground at Meitan Port on the way from Hankou to Yichang on the 13th of this month. Four or five attempts to tow it out were unsuccessful. Later, due to the shallow water level, the bureau sent workers to the site to remove the sand and mud around the Guangji's bow. On the 25th, the river level had risen by two feet, and the Hankou Bureau sent a ship to tow it out. It was successfully refloated at 10:00 AM yesterday and has been towed back to Hankou for major repairs.

Japanese Navy Has Left Shanghai: The 350 Japanese naval marines stationed in Shanghai, having completed their assigned term, have been ordered to return to the Sasebo Naval Corps in their home country. The transport ship Qingdao was specially dispatched to Shanghai to transport them. Yesterday at 10:30 AM, the Japanese naval officers and soldiers of the contingent boarded the ship at the Huishan Wharf and set sail. The replacement troops had already arrived in Shanghai.

Most Conditions in the Bookbinding Industry Resolved 159

Wage, Apprenticeship, and Meal Expenses Issues

Mediation to be Held Again Tomorrow Morning

Over 20 workers from more than 150 Chinese bookbinding shops in this city, including Ma Hongji, went on strike twice over the modification of treatment conditions and wage increases. Work was fully resumed the day before yesterday. The Social Affairs Bureau convened a mediation meeting yesterday, and all issues except wages and apprenticeships have been resolved. The details of yesterday's situation are recorded as follows:

Further Mediation: The Social Affairs Bureau has mediated the treatment conditions of the bookbinding industry multiple times, and Articles (3) and (4) have been agreed upon and resolved by both parties. Yesterday at 9:00 AM, a mediation committee meeting was convened. The attendees were committee members Wang Guoxian from the Public Security Bureau, Lu Yinzhu from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Zhao Jialing and Ren Changfu, representatives from the Bookbinding Industry Union, and Ding Handong and Xu Hanqing, representatives from the Bookbinding Industry Association. The chairman was committee member Wang Bing, and the recorder was Wang Zhichin. Until 5:00 PM, the following issues remained unresolved: (1) wage increase, (2) apprenticeship, and (6) meal expenses. It was decided that a further mediation meeting would be convened at 1:00 PM on the 28th with the Bookbinding Association, the Book Industry Association, and the Bookbinding Workers' Union.

Resolved Articles: The following articles have been agreed upon and resolved by both labor and management: (5) Workers' dining and lodging hall, apprentices have freedom in accordance with the workshop rules; (7) All memorial days stipulated by the National Government are to be observed with wages paid as usual (Western-style holidays are compensated on Sundays). If the employer wishes the workers to work, wages are to be doubled, and piece-rate workers are to be given an additional four dimes per day. Western-style workers have one day off every Sunday. If the employer wishes to work, an additional two dimes per person must be added with the consent of the labor side. The New Year holiday at the end of the lunar year will be from New Year's Eve to the fourth day of the New Year, totaling five days. Work must begin on the fifth day; (8) Wage exchanges are to be calculated in silver dollars according to the market rate; (9) The labor side will withdraw the issue of collecting union dues on behalf of the union; (10) The dismissal of workers and the closure of workshops are to be handled in accordance with government laws and regulations; (11) Male and female workers who encounter marriage (themselves) or funeral (parents, wife) events will be given one week of leave within the city and two weeks outside the city, with wages paid as usual (if there are special reasons, the leave may be extended as appropriate). Female workers will be given six weeks of leave before and after childbirth, and a childbirth allowance of 15 yuan will be provided. Female piece-rate workers will be given a midwifery allowance of five yuan. If the worker does not return after the expiration date, wages will be deducted on a daily basis. If the worker does not state a reason after two weeks, she will be dismissed unconditionally. The above-mentioned female workers must have worked for at least ten months to be eligible for this right. Apprentices and piece-rate workers are not subject to this rule; (12) Apprentices' monthly allowance is one yuan per month in the first year, two yuan per month in the second year, and three yuan per month in the third year. After completing the apprenticeship, an additional eight yuan will be added. Working hours are the same as for workers, with the same rest periods. Apprentices' cleaning and miscellaneous work is limited to a maximum of one hour. If workers do not have night work or Sunday work, apprentices may not work alone. Workers who eat their own meals during night work will be given a meal allowance. Apprentices who work night work for more than half a month will be given a subsidy of one yuan; those who work for less than fifteen days will not be given a subsidy. The treatment of apprentices during the apprenticeship period is the same as above. After completing the apprenticeship, the terms will be determined by both parties; (13) Customs: All year-end banquets, festivals, wine, food, and rewards, etc., must be conducted in accordance with the Gregorian calendar; (14) The labor side will withdraw the subsidy to the union; (15) Abolish the small contract quota system; (16) Each workshop must have separate male and female toilets, and the working area must be clean and hygienic; (17) and (18) No issues.

Suggestions from the Postal Workers' Union

People's Congress and Two Special Trade Union Laws 160

Submitted to the National Government for Reference

Notice to Members Yesterday

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union issued a notice and informed all members, stating that the Special Trade Union Law is the fundamental legal issue of the union. Since the promulgation of the Trade Union Law, the union has followed the draft proposal of 54 articles from the Preparatory Committee of the National Postal Workers' General Union and submitted it to the Central Government for approval, but it has not yet been promulgated, leaving the union and all special trade unions with no guidance for their work. Therefore, during the National People's Congress, comrades Zhao Shusheng and Qi Jiamou were sent to Beijing to join representatives from the Nanjing Postal Workers' Union and the Jiangsu Telecommunications Workers' Union to urge the worker representatives attending the People's Congress to submit the draft to the presidium of the congress. The presidium submitted it to the Fourth Proposal Review Committee of the congress on the 13th. After Comrade Chen Wenbin (member of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Workers' Union) strongly advocated for it, the committee decided to pass the principles and submit them to the National Government for reference. At the Eighth Meeting of the Congress, Comrade Peng Jiqun, the convener of the Proposal Review Committee, formally proposed the Special Trade Union Law and the National Trade Union General Organization Bill, and the congress resolved to pass them and submit them to the National Government for reference and consideration. In the future, the Central Government will definitely comply with the resolutions of the National People's Congress and implement and promulgate the Special Trade Union Law in the shortest possible time, so that the union can follow it and continue to work hard for the revolution and construction, develop its affairs, consolidate its foundation, and look forward to a brighter future. It is hoped that all members will appreciate the union's continuous hard work, be of one heart and one mind, be loyal and consistent, cherish the union, and work hard. This is the notice.

Depressed Situation in Silk Factories 161

Wage Restoration Unlikely to be on Schedule

The Shanghai Silk Factories Association convened a meeting of all executive committee members at 3:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included Wang Xiaolai, Wu Shenbo, Huang Jinfan, and ten others. Chairman Shen Huachen presided over the meeting. First, Chairman Shen reported that the issue of the distribution of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bonds had been decided by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, with Mu Ouchu, Zou Bingwen, and Song Ziliang appointed as committee members to distribute the bond amount and manage the fund. The inaugural meeting is scheduled to be held in Shanghai on the 29th of this month, and active preparations are urgently needed. Then, the committee discussed whether the wages of female workers could be restored to their original state. It was noted that this year's silkworm news in Jiangsu and Zhejiang had been severely affected by the weather. The cocoon production in Zhejiang was unusually poor, the cocoon quality was inferior, and the cocoon price was not cheap. In Jiangsu, most of the early and late silkworms died, and there was no hope for cocoon harvesting. Overseas silk sales still showed no signs of improvement, and silk prices were extremely low. The price of European and American Shanghai white silk factories was more than 400 taels different from the factory's cost, resulting in huge losses. Factories were unable to support themselves, and one-third of them had already shut down one after another. The more than 30 silk factories that are still operating are only temporarily maintaining the status quo. It is uncertain whether each factory will be able to continue working after the old cocoons are finished and the new cocoons are on the market, and how many silk factories in Shanghai will be open at that time. In short, the current foreign silk sales are so sluggish, and Japanese silk is being sold at low prices relentlessly. The factory price is small, and the cost is high. Even if the wages of each factory are not increased, it will be difficult to maintain them. The factories are facing so many difficulties and are all disheartened and negative. After a long time, no results were achieved, and the meeting was dismissed. It is feared that the restoration of the wages of female workers in Shanghai silk factories on June 1st will be difficult.

Cotton Cloth Reporting Industries

Responsibility for Dock Dues Collection and Payment 164

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce is Scheduled to Convene a Discussion Today

Regarding the issue of responsibility for dock dues collection and payment in the cotton cloth reporting industries, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau previously ordered the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to investigate and respond on customs. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce conducted a detailed investigation and reported that the dock dues should be borne by the merchants. The Social Affairs Bureau approved the report and ordered the three parties to coordinate and resolve the issue or contact each party separately to determine a proper solution and report it for review. It is reported that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is currently scheduled to convene a discussion today (27th). The details are recorded as follows:

Convocation Notice: Yesterday, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce notified the Cotton Cloth Industry Association, the Transportation Reporting Industry Association, the Sanshan Guild Hall, the Shanghai Merchants Association, the Shandong Guild Hall, and the Sichuan Merchants Association, stating that on May 22nd, a case was received from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau under number 10228, which opened an order to investigate and respond to the responsibility for dock dues collection and payment and requested review. The response was that the three parties should be convened to properly coordinate or contact each party separately to determine a proper solution and report it for review. Therefore, the three parties are scheduled to be convened at the association at 2:00 PM on May 27th to discuss and resolve the issue. A separate letter will be sent, and we respectfully request that you send representatives to attend on time.

Merchant Groups' Statement: Merchants from Andong, Longkou, Yantai, Dalian, Harbin, and other regions issued an important statement yesterday regarding the dock dues issue, stating that they have been purchasing and transporting cotton cloth to various provinces for more than 40 years. According to historical procedures, the dock dues, porterage fees, and other expenses are the responsibility of the owner of the goods. The merchants only know the market price and place orders accordingly, and have no need to be involved in other procedures. Furthermore, the freight owners have already added all expenses to the price of the goods. The power to increase or decrease prices rests with the freight owners. Now, it is forced upon the merchants to acknowledge the dock dues, which is tantamount to openly increasing and secretly taking, which is not only inconsistent with the facts but also contradicts historical procedures. The reporting industry is acting on behalf of the freight owners and has no reason to assume the responsibility. Although there are mediators mentioned in the newspapers, the truth is still unclear. Therefore, we are publishing this statement to clarify the responsibility of our business and the reasons for not being able to acknowledge the dock dues. We hope for clear understanding.

News from the Municipal Industrial Products Testing Laboratory 165

Since Dr. Shen Xiongqing took over as director of the Municipal Industrial Products Testing Laboratory (No. 4, Hehefang, Xiahui Road), the internal operations have been greatly expanded. Furthermore, an additional building at No. 3 next door has been leased. Craftsmen were hired to renovate it last month, and the work has now been completed. The number of commissions from various sectors is increasing daily, with dozens of items tested each month. Research problems such as polishing copper, lubricating oil, mimeograph paper, wax cakes, dry batteries, and badge coloring have all been started and will be successful in order. As for the certification issue, certificates have been issued for five items, including Aidulis Foreign Company's fertilizer, Baoxing Mineral Powder Factory's pencil lead, Taihe Hefen Factory's Hefen powder, Qi Minghe's colored hollow bricks, and Sanyu Industrial Society's silk yarn. It is also reported that the laboratory is currently standardizing the foot size and length of famous yarn silk socks produced by various sock factories in the city. Currently, the same size socks from each factory differ by as much as one to one and a half inches, making it impossible for buyers to choose. This is very inappropriate. The laboratory's deputy technician, Mr. Sun Zongshu, has visited various factories to investigate the situation of measuring socks and has now drafted a unified plan, which will be distributed to various factories soon to solicit opinions.

Two Trade Unions Retain Zheng Baozhao 167

Telegram Submitted to the Ministry of Railways

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Industry Consolidation Conference and the Beijing-Shanghai Section Transportation Workers' Union are alarmed that Zheng Baozhao, the deputy director of transportation of the railway, suddenly wants to resign. Therefore, they telegraphed the Ministry of Railways yesterday to retain him, stating that they were shocked to hear that Zheng Baozhao, the deputy director of transportation of the railway, had submitted his resignation to the ministry. Since Zheng assumed office a year ago, he has been supervising employees and focusing on railway affairs in order to develop state-owned production. The recent progress of the railway is a clear proof of this. All employees of the railway are now in the midst of supporting him, so the sudden news of his resignation is alarming. Therefore, we telegraphed the ministry to respectfully request that you do not approve his resignation in order to comfort the public.

Measures for Purchasing and Transporting Chilean Nitrate 168

Reviewed and Licensed by the Nitrate and Sulfur Bureau

The Ministry of Military Affairs of Nanjing sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating that in order to verify the use of Chilean nitrate in various provinces, all purchases and transportation by inland stores in the future will be reviewed locally by the provincial Nitrate and Sulfur Bureau for approval. The merchants and factories in your area that operate this business and prepare to use it themselves should report the annual import quantity and usage to the Nitrate and Sulfur Bureau for record. Within the approved limit, apply for transportation in accordance with the law. In addition to the statutory procedures for preparing documents and paying fees and stamp taxes, there are no other expenses. If there are difficulties or demands, merchants are allowed to report them to the ministry. The corresponding letter is hereby conveyed for your information and compliance.

Shanghai Anti-Opium Society Statement Regarding

Hunan Province's Seizure of the Anti-Opium Society 169

The news that the Hunan Anti-Opium Society was seized by the Changsha headquarters has drawn great attention from all sectors. According to the Chinese National Anti-Opium Society, the Hunan Anti-Opium Society was initiated by local people and has only been in the preparatory stage for a few months. The preparatory committee has inquired about the organization's methods and requested various assistance. The society has requested it to handle it in accordance with the organizational outline of local anti-opium groups, which stipulates that only those local groups that are directly organized by the society and have the participation of major local legal groups are recognized. The Hunan Anti-Opium Society is still in preparation, and the details have not been formally reported. As for the reasons for being seized and the background, they are not known. Since the society and the society have no systemic relationship, the society cannot be responsible for all actions. However, the news reports that the society was used by communists and falsely collected money are not true. The Local Merchants Association of Hunan, which is organized by local merchants, has always been deeply jealous of the anti-opium movement. The local authorities are also collecting special taxes. The matter is likely to be framed in order to eliminate the force against opium and achieve their goals of public cultivation, public transportation, and public sales. The society is waiting for detailed news and will take measures to respond. If the reports are true, the society will request the authorities to ban the society in order to maintain the anti-opium movement. If the reports are false, the society will provide assistance out of sympathy. The society is deeply concerned that the outside world is unclear about the fact that the society's anti-opium groups are only sympathetic organizations with no systemic relationship, so the Standing Committee has repeatedly resolved that local anti-opium groups should not use the name of anti-opium branch societies in order to avoid causing misunderstandings.

Transportation of Cocoons and Tea on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway 170

The Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway has been transporting cocoons and tea to the market. In order to maintain convenient and rapid freight transportation, the Railway Bureau's Transportation Department has approved the addition of vehicles to each freight train to load as much as possible. When there is freight congestion, special freight trains will be temporarily added to avoid hoarding. Therefore, this year's cocoon and tea transportation will not be delayed at the station. However, due to the increase in freight rates, many cocoon merchants have switched to shipping.

Songhu Road Changes Timetable 171

Effective June 1st

Since the relocation of the Shanghai Branch Line station to the east side of Baoshan Road on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway's Songhu Branch Line, transportation has become more convenient. However, the intermediate traffic seems to be uneven, so the Railway Bureau's Transportation Department is now working to improve it. It is estimated that the timetable will be changed on June 1st.

American Soldiers' Savagery 174

Two Chinese Stabbed 175

A Child Picked Up a Hat, Starting a Conflict

The peacemaker was stabbed instead.

Qu Shixiang, from Anhui, runs a clothing shop called Qu Shunji at No. 1229 Avenue Road, Gordon Road. At around 9:45 PM yesterday, the shop was already closed. Qu's son, Haigou, was playing on the steps in front of the shop when he saw three rickshaws coming from east to west. Two were carrying American soldiers in uniform, and the other was carrying a Westerner in civilian clothes. As the rickshaw passed the shop, the hat worn by one of the soldiers suddenly blew off and fell to the ground. Qu Haigou, being young and ignorant, bent down, picked up the hat, and threw it back to the owner. Unexpectedly, the soldier suddenly jumped out of the rickshaw and ran straight to Haigou. Without asking any questions, he began to beat him. A shop assistant named Ma, seeing this, became very angry and came forward to mediate. However, the American soldier not only refused to let go but also took out a small knife and began to wave it, stabbing Ma in the head, waist, and abdomen. The clothing shop owner, Qu Shixiang, was also caught in the crossfire while trying to resolve the situation, suffering head and left arm injuries and passing out on the spot. Many onlookers were angry but dared not speak out until the patrol officers arrived and reported to the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station. The Avenu Road Fire Brigade used an ambulance to send the two injured people to Baolong Hospital for treatment. The two soldiers who committed the crime were taken to the police station for questioning. The injured Qu Shixiang is 41 years old. He was stabbed in the left ear, and his left arm also suffered severe injuries. His assistant is 40 years old and was injured in the left ear and neck. The weapon entered the left side of the ear and penetrated deep into the throat, with a wound about seven or eight inches long, which is very dangerous. The abdomen wound could also be fatal. Qu Haigou, who picked up the hat, is 16 years old, and his injuries are minor.

The Old Site of Mingyuan Dog Racing Track

To Be Rebuilt into a New Amusement Park 176

With a Large Swimming Pool and Beach

And Equipped with Wave-Generating Machines

Plus a Beer Garden and Dance Hall

A Golf Course Is Also Included

The old site of the Mingyuan Dog Racing Track was officially announced yesterday by Mr. Bai Luoke, general manager of the Far East Theater Company, to be converted into a state-of-the-art amusement park to be opened within five or six weeks. It will be jointly operated by Mr. Bai and Mr. Hugh, a pioneer in the Far East film industry who has returned to Shanghai from Java. This summer, Mr. Ted, a carnival expert from Manila, will assist in Shanghai as a consultant. The park will be managed by another newly formed company, but the Mingyuan owner, the Dog Racing Association, will also hold a stake. The company name and capital amount have not yet been determined. It is said that the number of shares to be offered on the market in the future will be between 600,000 and 1 million taels. However, the site is already under renovation and is scheduled to be completed before the end of June. In the future, the park will have a large swimming pool, 160 feet long and 85 feet wide, with a beach and wave-generating machines. There will also be two orchestras. In addition, there will be a horse-racing moral German beer garden, a Japanese garden, a Chinese garden, a dance hall, and a golf course.

Also, it is reported that the dog farm built by the Dog Racing Association at the intersection of Haifang Road and Xiaoshadu Road, covering about 30 mu, has been sold to a Chinese businessman bank for 480,000 taels, a price of 16,000 taels per mu. The dogs in the farm have been merged into the Taopeng Road dog farm.

Five Russians

Angrily Destroyed Lenin's Portrait 177

Resisting the Police Led to Arrest

At 1:00 AM yesterday morning, five young Russians were passing by the Russian Consulate opposite the Licha Hotel on Huangpu Road. The building has been managed by the German Consul since the severance of diplomatic relations between China and Russia. After being handed over to Russian personnel last month, a portrait of Lenin was hung in the empty house. When the five Russians passed by, they hated Lenin because they had been stranded abroad. They broke in through the window and tore up Lenin's portrait. At that time, a Chinese police officer saw them and intervened. They refused to obey and resisted the Chinese police. Because they were outnumbered, they sounded the alarm. The five were arrested after police officers arrived. The names of the five Russians are Ai Wenximan, 20 years old, Xiyin, 16 years old, Pixiyin, 21 years old, Nuoweikefu, 17 years old, and Mai'erkefu, 18 years old.

Rushing River

A Young Man Commits Suicide for Love 178

Unknown if It Is Wang Weiyuan

A Letter of Affection Is Heartbreaking

At around 7:00 AM yesterday, a patrol boat from the Wusongkou Lifesaving Bureau recovered a male corpse in the Huangpu River opposite Yizhoutang. The man was about 20 years old, wearing a striped flannel jacket, white twill shirt and trousers, blue serge trousers, white socks, and a Zhigong ne shoes. He was immediately taken to the beach and reported to the Lifesaving Bureau. The local constable reported to the local court. At 4:00 PM, the Songjiang coroner arrived to examine the body. Since no relatives of the deceased could be found, the court took custody of the body for burial. When the corpse was recovered, a black leather folder was found beside him. Inside was a long-term pass for Shanghai Park with the name Wang Weiyuan on it. It is unknown whether this is the name of the deceased. There was also a receipt No. 10189 for a registered letter sent from Shanghai to Beiping on April 15, addressed to the Huabei Post Office in Beiping. There was also a suicide note, which stated that he committed suicide by jumping into the river due to a broken love. The original letter is transcribed below:

Dear, I picked up the pen to talk to you, but tears flowed uncontrollably instead of writing words. I'm heartbroken. I don't know what we are now and what to call you. If I write to you, will you ignore me? Do I have the face to do so? I keep thinking about it in my heart, so I wrote many letters and finally burned them with fire because I didn't dare to give them to you. Now I think everything is predestined and cannot be predicted by human power. We got the status of a loving, engaged couple, but we broke up due to some misunderstandings. It's really unexpected. The first day I came back, holding your jade hand again felt like a dream. When you were leaving, you tidied up the messy hair on my forehead for me, which showed that your love was as heavy as a mountain and completely revealed your loving heart. I will never betray your love. Tomorrow, you were walking by my side, and I said "Hello, Bai Xiang." This was because I loved you so much that I blurted it out. Who knew you would ignore me from then on. This repeated misunderstanding is even more unexpected. Now I have made up my mind to wait for you to take someone else's surname, let someone else take my surname, or go to the empty gate to repent and end my life. In short, I will always love you and never betray you. I will protect you when you are alive and bless you when you are dead. I wish you a bright future and boundless happiness in spirit.

Yawo Sha

The Township Head's Wife Was Kidnapped 179

Ransom of 5,000 Silver Dollars

Go to Da'an Port to Redeem the Ticket

At around 10:00 PM the night before, more than a dozen thugs speaking with a Northern accent and armed with handguns and Mauser pistols suddenly broke into the home of Wang Shiming, the head of Yawo Sha Township outside Wusongkou. They burst into the room and silenced everyone. They then split up to search the house. It was said that the bandits intended to kidnap a grain merchant named Gu. However, Gu's family happened to be celebrating a happy occasion that day, with many guests present, so it was inconvenient to take action. Since the township head, Wang, was not at home, they kidnapped the township head's wife, Zhou, and took her onto a bandit boat, sailing elsewhere. It is said that Township Head Wang runs a small shop in Beizhen, which is managed by Zhou. Zhou was planning to go to Shanghai the next day to purchase goods, so she had 600 silver dollars in cash, which were also taken away by the bandits. Yesterday, they received a letter from the bandits demanding a ransom of 5,000 silver dollars to be paid at Da'an Port in Jiangbei. Otherwise, there would be unfavorable consequences.

Shanghai West Assassination Case 180

Husband and Wife Both Suffered Misfortune

Husband Died, Wife Injured

Tan Genglin and his wife, local residents of Sanxin Garden, Yangjiata, about two li south of Wangjialou, Hongqiao, Shanghai West, were suddenly assassinated by enemies at around 2:00 AM on the morning before (25th). Villagers sent Mr. and Mrs. Tan to Shanghai Nursing Hospital on Robegen Road. Due to the severity of their injuries, they were transferred to Guangci Hospital on Jin Shenfu Road for treatment. Unfortunately, due to excessive bleeding, Tan Genglin died in the hospital at 6:00 PM. His wife, Tan Ji, suffered minor injuries and is not life-threatening. The details are as follows:

Deceased Family: The deceased, Tan Genglin, was 39 years old, a local resident of No. 94 Kangjiaqiao, south of Jinshi Great Temple on Kangnao Road, Shanghai West. He was very honest and hardworking and never argued with anyone. His wife, Ji, was 38 years old and had two sons and one daughter. The eldest son, Yongming, is 16 years old, the second son, Youyou, is 6 years old, and the daughter, Jingu, is 10 years old. His father, Tan Shunxiu, works in a foreign company. Six or seven years ago, Genglin and his friends Zhang Chunxiu, Zhang Fu, and others jointly purchased 7 mu of land in Bailongtan, south of Wangjialou on Hongqiao Road, and founded Sanxin Garden. Last winter, Genglin also purchased 3 mu of land near Yangjiata (about half a li from Bailongtan) and founded a garden solely. He built a simple bamboo fence around it and built two bungalows. The house number has not yet been assigned. Mr. and Mrs. Tan and their children moved into the residence immediately. Ji also helped her husband work, in addition to doing housework. The couple lived in harmony.

Assassination Situation: For some unknown reason on the 19th of this month, Genglin dismissed a servant named Jia, from Chongming. At about 2:00 AM on the 25th, three people each with weapons and flashlights broke into the house. Mr. and Mrs. Tan were awakened from their dreams. The assailants, without asking any questions, first stabbed Tan in the head and waist, totaling 13 stabs. He fell to the floor in a pool of blood. Ji was shocked and shouted for help and was beaten with an iron bar, causing bruises all over her body. The murderers, seeing that their goal had been achieved, fled in a hurry. Afterwards, neighbors Yang Mengzhou, Yang Muquan, Yang Genrong, and others carried Mr. and Mrs. Tan to Shanghai Nursing Hospital on Robegen Road. Due to the severity of the injuries, they were refused and transferred to Guangci Hospital on Jin Shenfu Road for treatment. Unfortunately, due to excessive bleeding, he died in the hospital at 6:00 PM on the afternoon before. Ji's injuries are relatively minor and are unlikely to be life-threatening.

Detained Suspects: After the incident, Pan Xueceng, the chief of the Hongqiao Township Police Station of the Sixth District One Branch, investigated and found that the deceased's family had two ducks, which were killed by Yang Zhiying, Yang Yuting, and others from Yangjiata on the fourth day of the second month of the lunar calendar this spring under the pretext of banning ducks, which caused a slight argument with the deceased. Therefore, Yang and others are suspected of being involved in Tan's murder, and they were arrested and sent to the Sixth District One Branch for further investigation.

Case of the Private Detective's Robbery of Morphine 181

Closing Arguments Concluded, Sentencing Scheduled

Liang Chengyu, a Chinese detective of the Second Section of the Inspector General’s Office of the General Police Department, was suspected of involvement in the robbery of morphine worth 50,000 silver dollars at the home of Li Liansheng, No. 439 Maleli, Chongqing Road, on July 28. He was detained by Western Inspector-General Yao Ke and sent to the Special District Court for two trials. Details were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. At around 1:00 PM yesterday, Judge Ge Zhitan took the seat in the Second Criminal Court for a continued trial. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated that since the case occurred, the police department had begun to investigate the stolen morphine, but there was still no progress. Li Liansheng's representative lawyer, E Sen, and the defendant Liang Chengyu's lawyers, Ye Fukan, Yuan Yang'an, Peng Xie, and others, appeared in court to defend him. According to Liang Chengyu, Li Liansheng, also known as Fang Liansheng or Xiao Liansheng, was known to him. Last year, when he lived in Dafangli, South Chengdu Road, Fang Liansheng also lived in the second house in the alley behind Baoyufang on that road, facing each other. After Li Huiqing was kidnapped, the Old Gate Police Department arrested the kidnappers Lu A’gen, Zhou Linsheng, and Zhou's mistress, Xu Yuying. The three confessed that Fang Liansheng was an accomplice. He had repeatedly tried to arrest him but failed to do so. This time, he was falsely accused due to a grudge. (Note: Lu A’gen has been sentenced to death, Zhou has been sentenced to life imprisonment, and Xu has been sentenced to 20 years in prison.) Li Liansheng denied being Fang Liansheng and having anything to do with the kidnapping case. Judge Ge examined the confession and observed that the judgment of the Lu A’gen kidnapping case contained Xu Yuying’s confession that she knew Liansheng. He then ordered the bailiff to bring Xu Yuying from the women's detention center of the Special Court to prove whether the Liansheng in this case was the same Liansheng in the kidnapping case. Before long, the defendant Xu arrived at the trial. She confessed that her name was Xu Yuying and that she knew Zhou Linsheng. One day, Lu A’gen and Liansheng came to my house to visit Zhou Linsheng, so I knew Liansheng. Judge Ge then ordered Xu to identify who Liansheng was in court. After a brief look, Xu pointed out Li Liansheng, but stated that she only knew his name was Liansheng and did not know his surname. At this point, the witness testimony was completed. Judge Ge announced that the closing arguments would begin. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin and defendant lawyers Ye Fukan and Peng Xie then stood up and argued with each other. Judge Ge then announced that the closing arguments of the case were concluded and that the sentencing would be scheduled for the afternoon of June 2. The defendant Liang Chengyu was returned to custody.

Resolution of the Case of Overseas Chinese Children Returning to the United States 184

The Shanghai Daily Press Association received a letter dated April 29 from Lin Shiheng, Chairman of the American Overseas Chinese Exemption Association, and Deng Zuyin, Director of the Executive Department. The letter stated that China and the United States are countries that can trade with each other, and merchants from both countries should have the freedom to travel to each other. However, recently, the United States has often restricted this right for Chinese merchants, especially the inability of Chinese merchants who entered after 1924 and their wives to obtain return permits, which is the most harmful. Because 80 to 90 percent of Chinese people enter with this qualification, if they cannot return to the United States after returning to China, the number of overseas Chinese in the Americas will decrease day by day and may eventually disappear. The overseas Chinese were worried and organized this association in 1929 by the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce of the Americas, the Ningyang General Association, the Zhaoqing General Association, the Gangzhou General Association, the Yanghe General Association, the Sanyi General Association, the Hehe General Association, the Renhe General Association, the Tongyuan General Association, the General Branch of the Kuomintang, the General Branch of the Constitutional Party, the Zhigong General Hall, the Christian Federation, and the Youth Association, with a total of fifteen major groups each sending two representatives to deliberate and proceed. They then selected Zuyin and Shiheng to go to Washington, D.C., to negotiate with the Ministry of Labor. Fortunately, the Ministry of Labor did not abandon them and issued Decree No. 13, allowing Chinese merchants and their wives to obtain return permits, which can be said to be a successful negotiation. However, the ministry subsequently explained that children of Chinese merchants who are 21 years old have reached adulthood and lose the qualification to obtain return permits. This interpretation is very different from what Zuyin and Shiheng requested when negotiating in Washington, D.C., and is not enough to comfort the overseas Chinese. Therefore, last year, the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce sent Zuyin and Liu Zhanbo to Beijing again to negotiate with the Ministry of Labor and request that it be revised. Zuyin returned to Shanghai and spent several months with Shiheng deliberating and seeking assistance from all parties so that the Ministry of Labor could make a satisfactory decision as soon as possible. It was finally approved on the 25th of this month and has been in effect ever since. Chinese merchants have benefited greatly from this, and the entire overseas Chinese community is extremely delighted. It is hoped that the comrades in your area also have the same feelings and should communicate with each other to investigate.

Shanghai Municipal Engineering Bureau Rectifies Road Administration 185

Dilapidated Houses at Sanpailou Wangyun Road Limited to Immediate Demolition and Construction

The Shanghai Municipal Engineering Bureau found that the houses at Nos. 2 to 18 Sanpailou and Nos. 9 to 37 Wangyun Road have been in disrepair for many years and are leaning and tilting. Examination of Dai Tingzuo's Body 192

Two American sailors, Brandel X. Secreper (transliteration), stationed on an American warship in the Huangpu River at the Xin Kai River wharf, hired a rickshaw at 3:00 PM on the 23rd to the Jinliyuan Wharf No. 8 warehouse of the China Merchants Bureau on the Bund of the French Concession. The Excellence of Huasheng Electric Fans 196

The Huasheng Electric Appliance Manufacturing Factory on Zhoujiazui Road, Hongkou, Shanghai, is a pioneer in China's electric appliance manufacturing industry. Established for many years, with rich experience, its various electric appliance products have long been praised by people from all walks of life. At this time, during the summer season, the electric fans produced by the factory are especially welcomed by society because of their many advantages. Here are some of them for the enjoyment of the people: The motor housing and base of the electric fan are made of steel, which is extremely strong, and painted with the best black paint. The wings are gold, and the base is lined with green, making the colors bright and beautiful. The speed of rotation is equipped with a three-speed switch. The high speed is 1,280 revolutions per minute, which shows the sufficiency of the wind power. The economy of electricity consumption is unmatched by any electric fan. For example, a 56-inch ceiling fan costs only one cent and six li of electricity per hour, a 16-inch table fan costs eight li of electricity per hour, and a 12-inch table fan costs five li of electricity per hour. Moreover, it can be used for any length of time without overheating, and is guaranteed for ten years. If there is no accidental damage, repairs will be free of charge. In this time of expensive gold and cheap silver, it is a great opportunity to promote domestic products. It is also heard that the factory's pricing of electric fans this year is particularly low in order to repay the enthusiasm of compatriots who love domestic products. For the convenience of customers, the factory has authorized major electrical material stores in this city and other places to sell its products.

New Large Warehouse of Zhejiang Industrial Bank 204

On North Suzhou Road

The Shanghai Zhejiang Industrial Bank has established three warehouses along the Suzhou River near the section to store collateral, stack goods, and handle passenger and freight matters properly. In recent years, the Shanghai market has been booming, and the need for cargo mortgages has been particularly high. The bank has noticed that the original warehouse buildings are old and has built seven five-story reinforced concrete warehouse buildings on North Suzhou Road along the Suzhou River to the east of the Old Garbage Bridge, which have been completed, covering an area of approximately seven acres. The front and back doors are both along the road, and the steel structure and ventilation ducts are all constructed using the latest methods. It is equipped with three of the latest elevators for loading and unloading goods. Insurance can be charged at the rate of first-class warehouses. The bank has also set up an insurance agency to provide insurance for goods stored in the warehouse. The warehouse rent is priced very reasonably. The warehouse has a branch so that goods stored in the warehouse can be borrowed from the branch if they need funds. All the equipment is designed to prioritize the interests of customers, making it the only warehouse of its kind in this city.
