The workers have always been peaceful, and the capitalists have no grievance or bitterness and the relationship is very good. Jinxin Factory Worker Representative Sanbao Huang Shengxiang.

Free Talk

World Tidbits 207

— Sea Guest

According to European zoologists, crocodiles have a long lifespan and can live up to ninety years.

The British Isles have 178,737 miles of roads, and if you drive a car on them, you can travel around the world six times.

Recently, two prize-winning Welsh foxhounds were auctioned in New York for the high price of £1,700. In Britain, these foxhounds are considered a good price at only £100 a pair.

Boot and shoe stores in England have recently started using small shark skin and frog skin to make boots and shoes. Small shark skin is very expensive and must be priced by the inch when purchased.

Fox hunting is very popular in several states in the eastern United States. Last year, there were 88 large hunts in North America, including three in Canada.

A British gentleman lost a malacca wood cane twelve years ago. Although his name was engraved on it, he could not find it anywhere. Last year, he suddenly found it on a train and it was finally returned to its owner.

A Record of the Amusing Farewell Party of Jiaotong University Teachers and Students 208

— Cheng Zhizheng

The class committee of the 20th class of Jiaotong University in this city, considering that the classmates of this class will soon leave the university and scatter in all directions, in order to unite feelings and permanently commemorate the occasion, held an unprecedented farewell party for all teachers and students of the university last Saturday evening. The party was full of interesting moments. I will describe one or two of them as follows:

The Shot Put King Performs Sparrow and Child: Lu Mingjun, the nationally famous shot put king, is also a classmate of this class. That night, he performed a song and dance drama, "Sparrow and Child," in which he played a small sparrow, while Zheng Ruhua and Chen Zhenrui, two gentlemen with large physiques, played the large sparrows and the child. It can be said that they exhausted their comedic talents. When they came on stage, the large and small sparrows each wore colorful costumes, sang, and danced gracefully. It is said that they had been practicing for several days. However, Lu, after all, is an athletic champion. In his vigorous dance, one could see his shot put, running, and basketball shooting postures. The audience cheered after each of the two acts.

The Water Escape of the Fine Arts School: That night, students from the Fine Arts School were also invited to perform magic, with more than ten acts, all of which were fantastically unpredictable. The most valuable were the live swallowing of burning charcoal and the water escape. The live swallowing of burning charcoal was performed by placing charcoal in the fire, and within a moment, the charcoal was red. The performer then put it in his mouth. In order to allow the audience to observe clearly, the performer walked to the bottom of the stage and performed it several times in the crowd. Everyone exclaimed in amazement. The last was the water escape. This magic trick is not common in China. A large bucket was filled with warm water and a person was put in it, covered with a lid and locked. After four minutes, the person came out leisurely. The skill was truly divine.

Two New Plays: Spoken dramas have recently become quite popular in Shanghai because they are more moving than Peking opera. That night, two plays were staged one after the other. One was "Suzhou Night Talk," directed by Mr. Pan Tinggan. The plot briefly describes a painter who encountered war in his youth and his home was burned. His wife and daughter were separated and he came to Suzhou alone to teach painting for a living. His wife and daughter also came to Suzhou later. The wife remarried a wealthy merchant, but unfortunately the merchant took a concubine, and the mother and daughter were abused. The mother soon passed away, and the daughter became a flower seller. One day, she happened to sell flowers at the painter's house and the father and daughter were reunited. Its intention is very profound. Ms. Wang Tongying, who played the flower seller, described the tragic past, and her expression was truly moving. Many women in the audience wept. Mr. Yu Shihuang, who played the old painter, was quite suitable for the role. The audience unanimously praised it as a great ethical construct. The other was "Poor Fika," directed by Ying Yunwei. The plot briefly describes Fika's love of drinking, and he was always drunk when he returned home. His wife was worried about him, so she discussed it with a doctor. One day, Fika was drunk again. The doctor ordered his wife to wear plain clothes and pretend that Fika was dead. Soon, Fika woke up and saw that everything in the room was different. His wife shed tears and called out to him, but he did not respond. A friend of his, a doctor, came and told him about his death. Fika was shocked and thought that he was dead. The doctor then proposed to his wife. Fika was angry and regretted it. He fell down and groaned. The doctor added sleeping pills to his face to make him lose consciousness. On the one hand, he restored everything in the room to its original state. Soon, Fika woke up and saw his beloved wife and the doctor attending to him. Only then did he realize that what he had seen just now was a dream. However, because the stimulation was too deep, he finally knew to cut off his ties with alcohol. Mr. Qin Shaoji, who played Fika, and Ms. Gu Meijun, who played Fika's wife, acted wonderfully and the meaning was particularly high.

Two Little Babies: The two sons of Mr. Du Dingyou, the director of the school library, were only four or five years old. Because of their excellent family education, they were also quite familiar with singing and dancing. That night, they performed on stage, lively and lovely, shining alternately with the sparrows and children performed by the Three Great Vajras, presenting a wonderful scene.

The Flourishing Bathing Buddha Festival 211

— Hongyan Guan Master

The Jing'an Temple in West Shanghai is one of the famous ancient temples in Shanghai. Every year on the eighth day of the fourth lunar month, the birthday of the Buddha, worshippers are like clouds. This year, this day happened to fall on a Sunday, and the general good men and women all came to offer incense. The incense fire was prosperous, and the number of visitors reached more than 20,000. There were more than 1,000 stalls selling domestic products along the area from Carter Road to Jing'an Temple. This year, the Ministry of Industry suddenly issued a notice restricting the establishment of stalls, so the stallholders were panicked and sought assistance from all parties. Zhifa, the abbot of the temple, also repeatedly argued and negotiated, and finally received a reply from the Ministry of Industry approving the establishment of stalls according to the old practice of previous years, so life was even more lively than in previous years. The crowd on Jing'an Temple Road was so large that it was like the "I can't walk, brother" in Hangzhou's incense boats. Tram passengers were crowded, and rickshaw drivers were gouging, charging four small oceans for what normally cost twenty copper coins from Carter Road to Jing'an Temple, no different from the gherkin sellers in Hangzhou's incense boats. Inside the temple, the former Guangdong Governor Li Guojun had a couplet that read: "Tin flies often close to the crane, the cup is passed without alarming the stork." On this day, the monks of the temple provided vegetarian meals for the followers. This flourishing bathing Buddha festival ended at sunset.

Travels Around the Yellow Sea (14) 212

— Huang Yanpei

I often say that Japan is able to continue the ancient Eastern civilization with the new Western civilization. Let me talk about the elegance of their customs. One day, I went to a bank to withdraw a remittance. Unexpectedly, it was a branch, and I had to go to the main branch to withdraw it. When I went out, I asked the doorman, "Where is the main branch?" I just asked casually, and the old gentleman became very happy, gesticulating for a long time, and I still stumbled. I took the wrong turn, and he finally led me for a long way until I saw the spire of the main branch in the distance before he stopped. Such enthusiasm is admirable. One day, I went with Mr. Zeng to visit a friend. After getting into the car, it had already moved several feet when someone ran up from behind and asked, "Did you lose a pen?" Mr. Zeng checked and knew that the pen was lost, so he replied, and the man asked, "What color is it?" He replied, "It's red." The man then led Mr. Zeng to the front of the police station and saw someone else holding a red pen high in his hand, walking towards the police station. A and B made contact and returned the item to its owner. It turned out that B saw the lost pen on the ground and, not knowing who it belonged to, picked it up and sent it to the police station. A, knowing who lost the pen, specially led him to retrieve it. Neither of these Japanese people hesitated to sacrifice their spirit and time to perform such duties for strangers. How could the cultivation of this kind of service spirit be achieved in a day or two? Another time, I was in Shenyang, looking for a suitable dry plate for the camera I brought. I asked several stores, and they all said they didn't have it. I entered a photo studio, and a Japanese man came out, inspected it, and said, "We don't have it, but I can look for it for you at other stores." Then he led me to many stores, and finally I managed to buy it before he said goodbye and left. He didn't make a penny of business, but he was willing to help people like this. I was so grateful to him that I was afraid of him. He was none other than a brave general who had won a hundred battles in the commercial battlefield!

All of the above can be said to be the good customs passed down from ancient times in the East, perhaps half of which are ideal. They are actually able to preserve and realize them. On the one hand, they have greatly absorbed Western material civilization in science.

I need to think deeply about this. It is a pity that this kind of virtue of people getting along with each other is extended to the international arena so that countries can also uphold justice, serve others, and help the weak and eliminate the strong. If all the commonly used methods of mutual suspicion, mutual jealousy, provocation, manipulation, deception, intimidation, fraud, and aggression are swept away, then it will be worthy of praise from all mankind.

A Farewell to Spring Tune

A strip of water, a thousand sails weave, a short stay in Penglai, spring has no trace. Tokyo and Xijing connect travel skirts, a thousand branches and ten thousand branches mark the national color. I come to the Eastern country when the flowers are just blooming, and by the time I return, the flowers have already withered. A lifetime of short dreams, spring comes and goes, in an instant, the bright mirror fades with red cheeks. There is no way to cherish the flowers and keep spring, craning my neck to look at the Eastern Emperor, silent and speechless. The guest's heart is busy straight for Qian Chun, the flower season is even more hurried than the tour schedule. I want to ascend the spring terrace, a crowd of beings, hand in hand, temporarily welcome each other. All who have blood and breath are like brothers, do not let them cook each other like beans. Once gone, the noble and the lowly are all equal, then people and things do not contend. When all beings are happy, the four seas are in spring, the flower world is long and affectionate. The lonely guest at the end of the world indulges in reverie, the trees are still like this, what about people? The Imperial Canal, a song, a double bridge, fallen flowers like snow, the sky vast and boundless.

Hawthorne's Detective Cases - Turning Point (26) 213

— Cheng Xiaoqing

He casually took out a pencil and wrote the number L. 72 in his diary. He continued, "I think that the white towel is not only very new, but also starched very stiffly, which shows that it was washed and ironed in a laundry shop. This number is probably written in the laundry shop for identification." I couldn't help but nod in agreement and said, "You are so careful! But I don't know how many laundry shops there are in Shanghai, which is several times more than the shops that sell Pearl Buck. What method did you use to investigate?" Hawthorne said, "This line is indeed more difficult. Fortunately, I have another auxiliary line." I asked in surprise, "Is there another line?" Hawthorne nodded and said, "Yes, don't you remember that when he used the trick of diverting the tiger away from the mountain, he called me to Zhe Shao Villa at No. 707 Datong Road? The location of Datong Road is very remote. If he didn't see the house number of Zhe Shao Villa often, how could he remember it so clearly? Therefore, I guessed that he must live on Datong Road, or at least pass by there often, so he remembered the house number of the villa very well. In a hurry, he couldn't think of another place, so he deliberately teased me with this villa where the coffin was sent. Because of this, I went to several laundry shops near Datong Road to investigate carefully. I inquired at nine shops and succeeded. The laundry shop is called Luhongji. The L is the abbreviation of the Pinyin of the word Lu. The number seventy-two is the number of their customers. So I knew that this person is called Che Shijie and lives at No. 11 Minquan Road, a horizontal road on the west side of Datong Road. Then I spent some effort to find out the history and current situation of this person. I also saw him once in person at the door of his house before I was sure that there was no mistake in this person. Later, I specially sent two people, one is Jin Sheng, who is guarding outside the Wen Lawyer's Office on Qingyun Road, and the other is Xu Hu, whom I borrowed from Zhang Baoquan, who is guarding outside Che Shijie's residence, and told them to report Shijie's whereabouts to me at any time. Until tonight, Jin Sheng called to inform me that Shijie had gone to the Carlton with a woman. I thought the time had come, so I implemented the plan I had prepared earlier. Are you satisfied with the way our encounter ended this time?" I couldn't help but pat Hawthorne on the shoulder and said, "Old friend, I really admire you twelve points! But this time, Che Shijie will definitely know that it was our revenge because of the return of the necklace. Then if he comes to look for us..." Hawthorne suddenly stopped me and said, "Don't worry, I originally wanted him to know before doing this. We are equally not liable under the law, so you don't have to worry. Isn't this your residence? Get out of the car quickly. Please say hello to your wife for me. If you are afraid that Che Shijie will come to take revenge again, if you have any preparation methods, that is another matter. Come to my residence tomorrow, and I will let you give full play to your abilities." (End)

Gold Price Sets New Record 215

Eight Hundred and Seven Taels

A Flying Leap of Twelve and a Half Taels. Yesterday, on the 26th, the gold price reached an unprecedented new peak of eight hundred and five taels or more. The silver market reported a decline, and there was a tendency to rise in the industry. However, the fluctuations were frequent, and the foreign exchange market was tight, with the exchange rate shrinking by one level. From the peak of the previous market to the subsequent decline, there was a difference of more than seven taels. The market later showed a soft but strong trend, with a difference of ten taels. It is now reported that the United States is selling silver, and the market has received this news, so the price has soared into the clouds. Because the exchange rate is increasingly tight, large investors on the trading floor have been actively buying, which ultimately led to a sharp increase of twelve or thirteen taels, which is irresistible. It is said that there is still the potential for a decline in the main bars this morning.

Foreign Exchange Trends are Tightening 216

Pegged Rates Continue to Shrink by One Level

Chinese Merchants Actively Buy British Gold

Yesterday, the British silver market was closed, and the US silver market was slightly longer. The market was flat, and HSBC's pegged rates had shrunk by one level. Automobile News

Special Article 227

The Principle, Structure, and Function of the Free Wheeling System 228

— Guoxiang

The principle of free wheeling is not new. England and France once experimented with it several years ago, but it failed to become popular on automobiles. Now, the American automotive industry has adopted this principle to improve the completeness of components and the economy of consumption. I briefly mentioned it in the first draft, and now I want to discuss this topic in three parts.

(1) Principle: The entire principle is the propulsive force generated by momentum. Observe a child riding a bicycle. When the speed reaches its fastest, the child suddenly stops pedaling. Logically, the speed of the bicycle should decrease greatly, but the bicycle still rushes forward extremely fast. Why is this? This is because of the propulsive force generated by momentum (see diagram CDE below, which indicates the thrust). On a bicycle, this component is called the flywheel. This principle has now been applied to automobiles.

(2) Structure: The free wheeling system is installed inside the gearbox. Its structure can be divided into two major parts (see arrow A in the diagram below, which indicates the installation of the free wheeling system): one is the outer casing, and the other is the inner core. When the free wheeling system is not working, these two parts are completely unrelated. Between the two, there are three conical raceways. Each raceway has a row of four steel balls that gradually increase in size. These four balls can run back and forth in the raceway (see diagram B below). The outer casing rotates with the force of the engine, and the inner core rotates the driveshaft, thereby transmitting power to the rear wheels. When the engine is driving the car forward, the three rows of steel balls (twelve in total) are forced to the narrow end of each raceway, connecting the engine and the rear wheels. When the carburetor throttle is closed, the engine immediately decelerates, and the outer casing also decelerates accordingly. At this time, the car's momentum drives the inner core to rotate, causing the steel balls to roll into the wide end of the raceway. Thus, the engine and the rear wheels are disengaged, but the car continues to move forward extremely fast. This entire process is natural and requires no clutch pedal, gear shifting, or other management.

(3) Function: The free wheeling system has many functions, which can be summarized into three: 1. Smooth vehicle operation; 2. Fuel economy; 3. Driving comfort.

1. Smooth Vehicle Operation: Ordinary three-speed and four-speed cars do not easily obtain engine braking force from second gear when descending hills. Installing a free wheeling system can provide this benefit, making downhill driving very smooth. Furthermore, shifting from second gear to third gear or from third gear to second gear does not require depressing the clutch pedal (although it is still permissible to do so), but the engine speed must be equal to or higher than the vehicle speed. The vehicle operates smoothly without any jolting. When the car approaches railway and highway intersections, simply move the free wheeling system to second gear to reduce speed and safely pass through. At the same time, it does not hinder acceleration and avoids any sluggishness. Regardless of the vehicle speed, gears can be changed at will. The car's four wheels are disengaged from the thrust, reducing slippage, which is especially beneficial on icy roads.

2. Fuel Economy: The most important saving is in the number of engine revolutions. Each time the free wheeling system engages, the engine stops working. On average, the engine only works for eight miles out of every ten miles driven. Driving 10,000 miles saves the engine 2,000 miles of work. According to tests by various companies, savings of 20% to 40% can be achieved. From this, it can be inferred that the engine's lifespan can be extended. Secondly, gasoline and lubricant are saved. When the free wheeling system is working, the throttle is closed, so gasoline can be saved by 12% to 20%. When the engine stops, lubricant can be saved by 20%. There are also considerable savings in regular vehicle maintenance, repairs, and engine decarbonization costs. Furthermore, using the free wheeling system extends the lifespan of various components in the car, such as the clutch, transmission, driving gear, rear axle, universal joint, and rubber tires.

3. Driving Comfort: After installing a free wheeling system, driving becomes easier, noise is eliminated, and the vehicle runs quietly, increasing driving comfort. Moreover, drivers are often overwhelmed and confused by the difficulty and complexity of managing automobiles, especially in heavy traffic, leading to anxiety, mental fatigue, and accidents. Those with free wheeling systems do not have these problems. With no complicated procedures to manage and no fatigue or mental confusion, they can move forward and backward freely and as desired. The benefits of the free wheeling system are significant.

Results of Six Car Tests by the Hupmobile Company

Horrific Automobile Accidents in the United States 229

— Gan

The United States is the most developed country in the automobile industry. Whether directly or indirectly, one in ten people relies on automobiles for their livelihood. However, the number of people who lose their lives in automobile accidents each year is also in the tens of thousands, which is truly shocking. According to a recent survey by the Travelers Insurance Company in Hartford, Connecticut, a total of 50,900 Americans died in automobile accidents in 1930. The shocking nature of this number is undeniable. According to the analysis, the day of the week with the most automobile accidents is Sunday, the time with the most accidents is between 5:00 PM and 8:00 PM, the weather is usually clear, and the location of the accidents is usually on flat, dry highways. Most of the cars involved in the accidents are privately owned, and most of the drivers are men with an average age of 39 and about one year of driving experience.

According to the above-mentioned survey report, the harm caused by automobile accidents is more severe than that caused by war. As for the cause of the accidents, driver negligence accounts for 68% of the total. Therefore, drivers are responsible for 84% of the deaths and 70% of the injuries and disabilities caused by automobile accidents. The report also clearly states that the harm caused by automobile accidents is more severe than that caused by war. Specifically, 50,510 American soldiers died in 18 months during World War I, while the number of deaths caused by automobile accidents in 1930 and the second half of 1929 reached 50,900. Is this not more severe than the harm caused by war? According to the analysis of the report, there were a total of 835,250 automobile accidents in 1930, resulting in 32,500 deaths and 962,325 injuries. Excessive speeding is a major cause of automobile accidents. Therefore, analyzing the deaths further, 8,146 people died from exceeding the speed limit, 3,241 people died from driving on the wrong side of the road, and 4,085 people died from disregarding traffic rules. Thus, driver negligence accounted for 85% of the 27,235 deaths.

Public buses accounted for a small percentage of automobile accidents in 1930. Among the 835,250 automobile accidents in that year, a total of 1,227,817 vehicles were involved. Of these vehicles, public buses were involved in only 331 fatal accidents and 8,337 non-fatal accidents. There are currently 95,400 public buses in the United States. Therefore, statistics show that only 9% of them are related to automobile accidents. Approximately 77% of the vehicles involved in accidents were privately owned cars, and this number accounts for 87% of the registered cars. Privately owned cars accounted for 78% of the deaths caused by automobile accidents. Commercial vehicles other than public buses accounted for only 15%. 45% of the accidents involved two cars colliding, and 46% involved cars colliding with pedestrians. 42% of the fatal automobile accidents occurred at intersections. However, the number of deaths was higher in accidents that occurred on roads. All the cars involved in the accidents that resulted in 32,500 deaths were in perfect mechanical condition.

News

Guizhou Province Transportation Company Expands Routes 230

The provinces of Yunnan and Guizhou in our country have mild climates and abundant products, making them prosperous regions. However, due to the obstruction of mountains and the inconvenience of transportation, everything is still in its infancy. During the 16th year of the Republic of China, Mr. Xiong and other gentlemen from Guizhou Province gathered large amounts of capital to establish a large-scale pioneer transportation company and set up branch stations in Tongzi, Zunyi, and other places. They specially sent people to Shanghai to purchase vehicles. After careful consideration, they decided to purchase ten Dodge special trucks managed by the American China Motor Company in Shanghai. It was originally planned to ship them immediately, but due to the impact of the political situation at the time, it was not until the 19th year of the Republic of China that people were sent to Shanghai to load and transport them. There were ships that could travel from Shanghai to Chongqing, but the route from Chongqing to Guizhou was mountainous and rugged. Even walking on foot was difficult, let alone these heavy cars. Therefore, during transportation, the managing company devised a way to dismantle each vehicle and pack it into more than a hundred boxes. The company also sent many mechanics and technicians to Guizhou to reassemble them after arriving in Guizhou. They departed from Shanghai in the middle of last summer and arrived in Guizhou after more than sixty days. Although it has only been in operation for half a year, the results have been remarkable. A shareholder meeting was held last month, and it was decided to extend the routes and add vehicles. They ordered twelve more Dodge cars from the China Motor Company. At the end of last year, due to the large number of passengers, there were not enough vehicles. They had added several other types of trucks in Guangzhou, but the results of their use were not as durable as Dodge. Therefore, this time, they unanimously advocated adding more Dodge cars.

Translations from Abroad

Two Anecdotes from the Automobile World 232

— Pei

The World's Most Precious Gemstone Automobile: The Kansas City Automobile Dealers Association in the United States recently commemorated its 25th anniversary by decorating a Pierce-Arrow sports car with precious gems, totaling a value of $125,000. This is unprecedented in automobile decoration. To commemorate the 25th anniversary, the entire car is silver in color. The curtains, cushions, and other accessories are made of specially crafted green leather. The car hood, chassis, and rods are all decorated with precious stones, which are extremely valuable, exceeding $100,000. The diamond decorations are particularly dazzling. In terms of value, this car is more luxurious than the Pierce-Arrow car commissioned by the King of Persia, which was entirely carved from gold and platinum and was of inestimable value. Therefore, when it was displayed, sentries and detectives were specially deployed to protect it and prevent accidents. However, enthusiasts still regretted not being able to touch it. This gemstone masterpiece was recently shipped to India, where it was one of the prized decorations at the royal automobile exhibition. The attending kings of India all praised this car as a rare treasure that they had never seen before. The entire body of the car is a dazzling red, using lead sheets.

European Actress Travels Alone by Car: The famous European actress Tessa Ailing recently traveled 1,800 miles in Europe alone in a Morris automobile. Her experience is quite interesting because she did not encounter any difficulties along the adventurous journey. Ailing drove herself from Gouck to Alaxuehua and then returned to the starting point, completing the entire journey. The most difficult part of the journey was driving 833.5 miles in 27 hours, resulting in an average speed of 30 miles per hour. On the return trip, Ailing did not take the old road but chose a difficult mountain road around the Alps before reaching the starting point. From Grass to Glaneau, there were six rugged mountain roads, the lowest being 1,774 feet and the highest reaching 3,858 feet. In addition, the journey was fraught with wind and snow, and the cold was unbearable. The windshield was covered with ice and snow for fifty miles, forcing Ailing to lean out of the car to drive, exposing half of her body to the cold. The road up the mountain was extremely steep and covered with snow, making driving very difficult. Fortunately, the Morris car was built solidly and did not malfunction. Its automatic ignition system was also very satisfactory. Therefore, although the 1,800-mile journey was under extremely harsh weather conditions, Ailing was able to overcome the difficulties because of her courage and superior driving skills, as well as the excellent quality and durability of the Morris car.

German Benz Sports Car Wins Victory at the Italian 1,000-Mile Automobile Race

Overseas Road Administration Anecdotes 233

— Wu Can

The Beauty of French Highways: Within dozens of miles around Paris, France, there are national highways connected. These national highways are nearly a hundred feet wide and paved with asphalt. Large trees are planted in two rows on each side of the road. In the spring and summer, the green leaves provide shade, making driving very elegant. The scenery on both sides is even more beautiful. Because the streets in Paris are orderly, the intersections are particularly lovely. The square of the Arc de Triomphe has twelve roads intersecting to form a circular shape. The majestic Arc de Triomphe can be seen from any angle. The surrounding streets intersect to form a rectangular square. The layout is exquisite, and there are gardens. Each route is designated to avoid confusion. The buildings on the other streets of Paris are also uniform and orderly, which is also very beautiful.

The Improvement of Dutch Highways: Although the Netherlands is a small country with an area of 34,190 square kilometers, its population density is very high, with a total population of over 7,737,000, or 226 people per square kilometer. A recent examination of the country's transportation situation reveals that the lack of good roads is still in its infancy. Although automobile transportation has become widespread, the poor condition of the roads makes improvement necessary. The total length of its roads is 25,000 kilometers, of which 2,000 kilometers are national roads, 3,000 kilometers are state roads, and 20,000 kilometers are village roads. Roads are classified into three levels: the first level has an excellent road base and cables and is flawless for transportation; the second level is well-constructed and capable of handling general transportation; and the third level is poorly constructed and of little transportation importance. Only about 700 kilometers of national roads belong to the first level, and very few belong to the second level, only about 1,300 kilometers. Most of the third-level roads are in remote areas. Therefore, improving road transportation is essential to meet the frequent needs.

Brazilian Highway Fund: Brazil is a large country in South America. Until 1927, its road administration was solely under the jurisdiction of the state governments. The central government only took the form of supervision, but it did not establish a special agency for road supervision. Later, as the value of roads gradually increased, the general public believed that improving roads was an urgent matter. The government then established a road bureau within the Ministry of Agriculture, Commerce, and Industry to study road transportation. Since January 1928, it has implemented construction-related financial measures. The implementation and maintenance of the measures were also formulated and announced. The Road Bureau was established, and all matters related to this were transferred to the newly established Road Bureau. The collection of funds is specialized in the collection of a certain percentage of surtax on the import tax of gasoline, automobiles, car chassis, tires, automatic bicycles, and automobile accessories. The funds are used to cover the initial annual amount of 4,672,000 yuan. The tax revenue in 1927 was only 2,553,652 yuan. Because the law was implemented late, only half of the revenue was collected.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions 234

(1) Articles should be limited to introducing the latest domestic and foreign publications. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, and other books and newspapers are included. Trivial books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Illustrations should be limited to recent works by new domestic and foreign artists and attachments related to the text.

(3) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Books and photographs should be related to the text.

(5) Articles should not exceed 3,000 characters.

(6) Manuscripts should not be written on both sides of the paper.

(7) Drawings should not be drawn with blue ink and should not be drawn on colored paper. White paper and black ink should be used.

(8) Please indicate "Book and Newspaper Introduction Editor Receives" on the manuscript.

(9) Manuscripts will not be returned whether they are published or not. If you need them to be returned, please state this in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) Compensation for articles is three yuan, two yuan, or one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to drawings and photographs. Special manuscripts will be compensated separately.

Social News

Foch's Diary of the European War, Translated by Gu Angruo 235

Our gunners were all killed, with no ammunition and no soldiers left. The entire ship was filled with smoke and fire. The captain, wanting to save the surviving crew members, steered the ship towards the shore.

I was in the engine room on the starboard side, which had already caught fire. When we received the order to open the seacocks and go to the deck, the engine's crankshaft had already struck the water's surface, turning into white foam. We followed the order, but the enemy's artillery fire had destroyed the engine room beyond repair. Out of twenty people, only two were able to follow the order and go to the deck; the rest were either killed by the artillery fire or lost their lives from the boiling water shooting out of the ruptured steam pipes. I and an older petty officer were exceptionally fortunate to escape the disaster. I almost lost my life from the surge while opening the seacocks, but luckily, a stream of oil saved me.

The clothes on my body were completely torn apart. At first, I didn't realize I was naked until I reached into my pocket and realized I was completely bare. The fact that I had no pockets and no clothes made me very embarrassed.

I climbed onto the deck from a hole. Shells were still exploding everywhere. Through the thick smoke and flames, I saw huge waves rushing towards the deck. I thought we were certain to be completely submerged. Others may have had this thought as well, because they jumped into the water, away from the sinking ship. Just as I was about to follow them, it seemed as if my guardian angel stopped me from jumping into the water. I turned around, went through the smoke and flames, and went to the starboard side, where Captain Maulu was rescuing the injured. The smoke and flames were slightly less intense than before. Everyone cheered, seemingly forgetting everything. We saw our flag fluttering at the top of the mast. At this moment, a wounded and bleeding soldier staggered forward from beside a destroyed cannon, shouting, "Three cheers for the captain!" In an instant, this man fell to the deck. This soldier was permanently silenced.

April 6th. German troops occupied the French Sixth Army's positions west of Saint-Gobaain, between the Oise River and the Aisne Canal. The Sixth Army had already anticipated this battle on the enemy's side. Although the Sixth Army had penetrated deep north of the canal, it was only guarded by a few outposts. Therefore, the German troops advanced in scattered formations. They retreated upon seeing the battle. However, the enemy advanced cautiously. It took four days to advance to the Aisne Canal (April 6th to 9th). (To be continued)
